{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_AND_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Acknowledging subject's disclosure and maintaining rapport", "tone_constraint": "Accepting, non-threatening, and permissive", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a pacing statement followed by a truism regarding the subject's willingness to share."}, "instruction": "내담자가 무언가를 말하거나 반응했을 때, 그들의 협조를 긍정하면서도 동시에 그들의 심리적 경계와 자율성을 존중하는 밀턴 에릭슨 식의 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여 응답하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 'All right'이라는 표현을 통해 내담자의 이전 발화나 행동을 즉각적으로 수용(Pacing)하여 라포를 강화합니다. 이어지는 'Now'는 주의를 현재의 순간으로 전환시키는 앵커 역할을 합니다. 핵심 문장인 'there are a lot of things that you are willing for me to know'는 거부할 수 없는 사실(Truism)을 진술하는 것입니다. 이 문장은 내담자가 정보를 제공하고 있다는 사실을 긍정함과 동시에, '말하고 싶지 않은 것'이 있을 수 있다는 내담자의 무의식적 저항이나 비밀을 가질 권리를 간접적으로 인정해 줍니다. 이는 내담자로 하여금 자신이 통제권을 쥐고 있다는 느낌을 갖게 하여 방어 기제를 낮추고, 역설적으로 더 깊은 소통으로 나아갈 수 있는 안전한 심리적 공간을 마련합니다.", "output": "All right. Now there are a lot of things that you are willing for me to know."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Exploring the client's hidden or private information (secrets).", "tone_constraint": "Curious, non-confrontational, and permissive.", "structural_constraint": "An interrogative sentence focusing on quantity to bypass resistance regarding existence."}, "instruction": "내담자가 숨기고 싶어 하는 비밀이 있다는 사실을 자연스럽게 인정하게 만들면서도, 그 내용을 당장 말해야 한다는 압박감을 주지 않는 질문을 던지세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 저항(비밀을 지키려는 의지)을 정면으로 돌파하기보다는 우회하는 전략을 선택합니다. '비밀이 있습니까?'라는 질문은 '아니오'라는 거부 반응을 유발할 수 있으므로, 비밀이 존재한다는 사실을 전제로 깔아야 합니다. 'How many(얼마나 많은가)'라는 수량 형용사를 사용함으로써 내담자의 의식적인 주의를 '비밀의 유무'가 아닌 '비밀의 개수'로 돌립니다. 이는 내담자가 숫자를 생각하는 동안 무의식적으로 비밀의 존재를 긍정하게 만드는 전제(Presupposition) 기법입니다. 또한, 비밀의 내용을 묻지 않고 개수만 물음으로써 내담자의 방어 기제를 안심시키고 치료적 라포를 유지합니다.", "output": "How many things are there about you that you don't want me to know?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_INTERROGATIVE_SEARCH", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inquiry into the underlying cause of a subjective experience or state.", "tone_constraint": "Curious, gentle, and non-confrontational, yet psychologically provocative.", "structural_constraint": "A simple closed-ended question that functions as an open-ended psychological prompt."}, "instruction": "Ask the subject if they are aware of the reason behind their current experience, using a phrasing that triggers an internal search for meaning without demanding a logical explanation.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate a deeper level of introspection, I must use a question that appears simple on the surface but carries profound weight for the unconscious mind. By asking 'Do you know the reason why?', I am doing several things simultaneously. First, I am presupposing that a 'reason' actually exists, which gives the subject's experience a sense of validity and purpose. Second, I am not providing the reason myself; instead, I am inviting the subject to engage in a 'transderivational search' (TDS). This process forces the unconscious mind to scan its own internal database to find a meaningful connection or cause. The simplicity of the phrasing bypasses the critical, analytical mind which might try to argue or rationalize, and instead speaks to the part of the person that is experiencing the change or the state. It is a permissive way to lead the subject toward their own internal discoveries while maintaining a stance of humble curiosity.", "output": "Do you know the reason why?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_RESISTANCE_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Self-awareness and the exploration of repressed or avoided personal truths.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet protective, mysterious, and non-confrontational.", "structural_constraint": "Uses presuppositions, negative commands, and paradoxical questioning to bypass conscious resistance."}, "instruction": "내담자가 직면하기 싫어하는 내면의 비밀이나 저항감을 다룰 때, 그 내용을 강제로 말하게 하지 않으면서도 무의식이 그 존재를 탐색하도록 유도하는 에릭슨의 대화 기법을 사용하여 발화하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 'Now the important thing'이라는 문구로 주의를 집중시키고 뒤따를 질문의 비중을 높인다. 둘째, '알고 싶지 않은 것이 무엇인지' 묻는 역설적 질문을 통해 내담자의 내부 검색(Transderivational Search)을 유도한다. 셋째, 'Don't tell it'이라는 부정 명령(Negative Command)을 사용하여 내담자의 방어 기제를 안심시킨다. 말할 필요가 없다는 허용은 오히려 그 주제에 더 깊이 집중하게 만든다. 넷째, 'You don't want to know it'이라고 내담자의 거부감을 기정사실화하여 저항을 수용(Utilization)한다. 다섯째, '얼마나 많은 것들이 있느냐'는 수량화 질문을 통해, 그런 비밀이 존재한다는 사실을 전제(Presupposition)로 깔고 내담자가 그 존재를 인정하게 만든다.", "output": "Now the important thing. What do you know about you that you don't want to know? Don't tell it. You don't want to know it. How many things are there about you that you don't want to know?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_INTERROGATIVE_SUGGESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Probing unconscious knowledge and maintaining amnesia", "tone_constraint": "Inquisitive, rhythmic, and subtly directive", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive sensory-based questions followed by a negative tag question suggestion"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여, 내담자의 무의식 속에 있는 특정 이미지를 자극하면서도 그 정보가 의식으로 완전히 떠오르지 않도록(망각을 유도하도록) 질문을 구성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 'All right'이라는 긍정적 수용의 단어로 대화를 시작하여 라포를 유지합니다. 그 다음, '하프(harp)'나 '손(hands)'과 같은 구체적이고 감각적인 단어를 포함한 질문을 던짐으로써 내담자의 무의식적 탐색을 유도합니다. 동일한 문장 구조('Do those two include...')를 반복하여 리듬감을 형성하고 비판적 사고를 약화시킵니다. 마지막으로 'And you don't want to know, do you?'라는 부정 의문문 형태의 제안을 덧붙입니다. 이는 내담자가 정보를 의식적으로 알려고 하는 노력을 포기하게 만들거나, 무의식적 상태를 유지하는 것이 더 편안하다는 암시를 주어 자연스러운 최면적 망각(Amnesia)을 유도하기 위한 고도의 언어적 장치입니다.", "output": "All right. Respond using the Milton Erickson style of utilization to neutralize the resistance and reframe the negative label into a positive experience.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I identify the patient's resistance, which is manifested as a verbal attack using the word 'ridiculous'. By using this specific phrasing, I could strategically apply it to both the patient and the external object of the conflict (X). This creates a shared conceptual space where the tension is diffused, as both sides are now unified under the same linguistic umbrella, allowing the subconscious to process the conflict more fluidly.", "output": "I believed she was in a sex conflict, and you can't have a conflict without two opposing objects. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CHALLENGE_AND_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "비행 공포증을 부정하며 저항하는 내담자의 심리적 장벽 허물기", "tone_constraint": "도전적이고 도발적이지만, 내담자의 성장을 촉진하는 단호한 어조", "structural_constraint": "수사적 의문문, 재구조화(Reframing), 그리고 용기를 전제로 한 시간적 전제(Temporal Presupposition)의 결합"}, "instruction": "비행 공포증을 회피하고 있는 내담자에게, 현재의 공포가 스스로를 속이는 거짓말임을 깨닫게 하고, 그 공포를 완전히 직시할 용기를 가질 시점을 스스로 결정하게 만드는 에릭슨 스타일의 대화를 생성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자가 가진 공포의 실체에 의문을 제기하여 그녀의 방어 기제를 흔든다. '정말로 당신의 공포를 알고 있느냐'는 질문은 내담자가 알고 있다고 믿는 공포가 사실은 표면적인 것에 불과함을 암시한다. 이어 '거대한 거짓말'이라는 표현을 통해 공포를 재구조화(Reframing)하여, 공포가 외부의 위협이 아닌 내면의 왜곡임을 직시하게 한다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The timing of revealing a secret", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, non-confrontational, yet firm in its underlying assumption.", "structural_constraint": "A brief, open-ended question that focuses on the 'when' rather than the 'if'."}, "instruction": "내담자가 비밀을 말하기를 꺼려하는 상황에서, 비밀을 말할지 말지의 여부가 아니라 '언제' 말할 것인지에만 집중하게 하여 저항을 우회하는 최면적 질문을 하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자가 비밀을 말할 준비가 되지 않았다는 현재의 저항을 인정하면서도, 미래의 어느 시점에는 반드시 말하게 될 것임을 기정사실화(Presupposition)한다. 둘째, '비밀을 말하겠습니까?'라는 폐쇄형 질문은 거절의 선택지를 주지만, '얼마나 나중에?'라는 질문은 거절의 가능성을 배제하고 오직 시간적 간격만을 선택하게 만든다. 셋째, 이는 내담자에게 선택의 자유를 주는 것처럼 보이지만, 실제로는 무의식적으로 '말한다'는 행위를 수용하게 만드는 이중 구속(Double Bind)의 변형이다. 넷째, 매우 짧고 단순한 질문을 통해 내담자의 의식적인 비판적 사고가 개입할 틈을 주지 않고 무의식에 직접적으로 '나중에 말할 것'이라는 암시를 전달한다.", "output": "How much later?"}

'ought you?'라는 부가 의문문 형태를 사용하되, 일반적인 'should'보다 강한 도덕적/내적 당위성을 암시하는 'ought'를 선택하여 내담자의 자아 이상(Ego Ideal)을 자극함. 4. 일반적인 의문문 어순을 비틀어 순간적인 혼란(Confusion)을 유도하고, 그 틈에 무의식이 답변을 탐색하도록 설계함. 5. 'Are you?'라는 짧은 질문은 술어가 생략되어 있어, 내담자는 무의식적으로 그 빈자리를 자신의 현재 상태나 문제로 채우게 됩니다. 이는 '초월적 유도 탐색(Transderivational Search)'을 유발하며, 내담자가 자신의 존재론적 질문에 직면하게 만듭니다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_NEGATIVE_TAG_QUESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reducing the emotional intensity of a patient's embarrassment regarding their symptoms.", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, leading, and subtly authoritative while appearing inquisitive.", "structural_constraint": "A negative statement followed by a tag question to facilitate agreement and bypass resistance."}, "instruction": "Create a conversational hypnotic intervention to help a patient acknowledge that their embarrassment has diminished, using a negative tag question and a temporal marker.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Identify the target emotion: The patient feels embarrassed about their symptoms. 2. Apply a temporal shift: Use the word 'now' to distinguish the present moment from the past, implying that change has already occurred. 3. Use negative suggestion: By saying 'isn't so embarrassing' instead of 'is comfortable,' I bypass the conscious mind's tendency to argue, as the brain must first process the concept of embarrassment before negating it. 4. Soften the delivery with a tag question: Adding 'is it?' at the end transforms a direct assertion into a gentle invitation for the patient to search their internal experience and find the truth of the statement, leading to a self-validated reduction in shame. 5. Strategy - Dissociation: Separate the 'conscious' (which is resisting) from the 'unconscious' (which is capable). 3. Strategy - Utilization: Frame the hypnotic response not as a submission to the therapist, but as a 'yielding' to an internal 'need' of the unconscious. 4. Linguistic Choice: Use 'know what to do and how to do it' to instill confidence in the internal process without specifying the 'how,' which avoids triggering critical analysis. 5. Contingency (The 'When-Then' bridge): Link the act of 'giving full expression' (the hypnotic work) to the 'recovery from the present problem' (the client's goal). This makes the client's desired outcome dependent on their cooperation in the trance state. 6. The strategy is not to ignore the symptom, but to 'translate' it. I will use the concept of 'avenues of experience' to suggest that the mind has multiple pathways. By shifting the problem from a rigid conscious framework to the vast reservoir of 'experiential learnings'—skills the patient has already mastered in other contexts—the problem becomes solvable through existing resources. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISSOCIATION_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The inherent wisdom and processing power of the unconscious mind.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet supportive, calm, and deeply reassuring.", "structural_constraint": "A concise declarative sentence utilizing a clear dissociation between the 'unconscious mind' and the 'conscious self' (you)."}, "instruction": "Explain to the listener that their internal, non-conscious processes are far more capable and knowledgeable than their conscious awareness, aiming to reduce conscious resistance and foster trust in their inner resources.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the therapeutic goal of empowering the patient's internal resources, I must first create a linguistic separation between their struggling conscious mind and their capable unconscious mind. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_IDEOMOTOR_LINKAGE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Sexual dysfunction treatment through sensory anchoring", "tone_constraint": "Calm, matter-of-fact, and reinforcing unconscious autonomy", "structural_constraint": "Linking a current involuntary tactile sensation to a future physiological response"}, "instruction": "내담자가 현재 느끼고 있는 머리카락의 촉감을 활용하여, 이를 성적 기능의 회복과 연결하는 무의식적 닻 내리기(Anchoring) 암시를 작성하십시오. 내담자의 손 움직임이 불수의적임을 강조하고, 이 감각이 향후 신체적 반응을 유도하는 트리거가 될 것임을 명시하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 현재 집중하고 있는 '머리카락의 감촉'이라는 감각적 사실(Truism)에서 시작합니다. 그 다음, 손의 움직임을 '멈출 수 없다'고 묘사함으로써 의식적 의도보다 강력한 무의식적 관념운동(Ideomotor response)을 유도하고 저항을 무력화합니다. Nothing can tell you that."}

By initiating a process—such as lifting toward the face—I create a kinetic and mental momentum. This minimizes the shock and bypasses the immediate defensive mechanisms by making the transition feel like a natural extension of an already unstoppable process.", "output": "I initiated the process of lifting toward his face and hair. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_FUTURE_PACING_SAFEGUARD", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Integrating and accepting intense personal desire", "tone_constraint": "Confident, reassuring, and predictive", "structural_constraint": "Future tense framing with immediate reassurance and repetitive reinforcement"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 강렬한 욕망을 두려워하지 않고 수용하면서도, 사회적/윤리적 선을 넘지 않도록 안심시키는 미래 지향적 암시를 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자는 자신의 욕망(desire)이 가진 강도(forcefulness)에 대해 통제력을 잃을까 봐 두려워하거나 거부감을 느낄 수 있음. 2. 이 강렬함을 '기쁨(delighted)'의 원천으로 재정의(Reframing)하여 긍정적인 에너지로 전환함. 3. 동시에 '상대방을 불쾌하게 하지 않을 것(not offend)'이라는 명확한 경계선을 설정하여 내담자의 도덕적 저항이나 불안을 사전에 차단함. 4. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PERMISSIVE_SUGGESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Invitation to view a personal collection", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, authoritative, and curiosity-inducing", "structural_constraint": "A permissive question using a superlative to frame the value of the experience"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 스타일로 내담자의 호기심을 자극하고 라포를 형성하기 위해, 당신의 독특한 개인 수집품을 보여주겠다는 제안을 담은 질문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자의 주의를 문제로부터 돌려 새로운 경험으로 유도하기 위해 '호기심'이라는 자원을 활용하기로 결정함. '세계 최대의 개인 소장품'이라는 최상급 표현을 사용하여 제안의 가치를 극대화하고 내담자의 무의식적 기대를 고조시킴. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_RAPPORT_BUILDING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Explaining social invitation through shared interests", "tone_constraint": "Matter-of-fact, simple, grounding", "structural_constraint": "Short declarative sentences with repetition of preferences"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 스타일로, 특정 인물을 초대한 이유를 구체적이고 감각적인 공통 관심사를 나열하며 설명하여 자연스러운 유대감을 형성하는 발화를 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 초대의 이유를 추상적인 논리가 아닌 구체적인 사물(굴, 목조각)에 대한 선호도로 치환합니다. 이는 내담자나 청취자가 반박할 수 없는 사실(Truism)을 제시하여 'Yes Set'을 형성하기 위함입니다. 'He likes... and so do I'라는 대칭적 구조를 사용하여 두 인물 사이의 심리적 동질성을 언어적으로 형상화합니다. 마지막으로 'We share likings'라는 단순하고 명료한 결론을 통해 복잡한 사회적 관계를 근본적인 '공유'의 개념으로 환원시켜 무의식적인 수용을 유도합니다.", "output": "He knows I like oysters and he likes wood carvings and so do I. We share likings."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CLINICAL_MAPPING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Emotional dynamics and family systems in anorexia nervosa", "tone_constraint": "Clinical, authoritative, and deeply perceptive of unconscious undercurrents", "structural_constraint": "Progressive movement from external family dynamics to internal psychological defenses, ending with symbolic unconscious identification"}, "instruction": "Analyze the psychological and familial underpinnings of anorexia nervosa in adolescent girls based on clinical experience, focusing on the hidden emotional conflicts.", "reasoning_trace": "To provide a comprehensive clinical picture, I first establish empirical authority by citing a specific number of cases (about fifty), which grounds the observation in long-term experience. I then shift the focus from the individual patient to the family system, identifying the 'peculiar emotional relationship' as the primary context of the pathology. I map the parental emotions as a complex duality of repressed anger and overt anxiety, creating a confusing environment for the child. Moving to the patient's internal state, I describe the symptoms—passivity and starvation—not as mere behaviors, but as a profound defense against 'emotional involvement' itself. I specifically isolate the fear of the mother as a key clinical feature. Finally, I delve into the deepest layer of the patient's psyche, identifying a 'messianic purpose' or poorly verbalized religiosity. This symbolic framing explains the patient's ability to override the biological drive for hunger, as the starvation is unconsciously transformed into a form of spiritual or sacrificial identity.", "output": "In all cases I have known of anorexia nervosa in children (about fifty, and all girls from ages nine to fifteen) there has always been a peculiar emotional relationship between the parents and the patient. It is one of concealed, repressed anger, resentment, and extreme frustration together with anxiety, concern, and fear on the part of the parents. For the patient the emotional behavior is most difficult to describe. There appears to be an underlying state of fear of all emotional involvement manifested by a submissive passivity, total lack of self-concern, the rejection of food to the point of death by starvation, a concealed fear of the parents, particularly of the mother, and repression of hunger feelings and all autocritical faculties. Underlying all of this is a vaguely conceptualized religiosity suggestive of a poorly formed and often not verbalized identification with a messiah or a messianic purpose."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_SHOCK_AND_PARADOX", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Initial intervention for an eating disorder involving family dynamics", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, blunt, and strategically provocative to break existing patterns", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a sharp command to the parent to disrupt the power dynamic, followed by a paradoxical statement to the child"}, "instruction": "거식증이나 식사 거부 문제를 가진 딸과 그 어머니를 상담할 때, 어머니의 간섭을 차단하고 딸에게 식사에 대한 통제권을 돌려주어 저항을 무력화하는 에릭슨 식의 초기 개입 방식을 보여주세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자(딸)의 증상을 강화하고 있는 어머니의 과도한 개입을 즉각적으로 차단하기 위해 '충격 요법(Shock Technique)'을 사용합니다. '입 다물라'는 거친 표현은 사회적 통념을 깨뜨려 상담의 주도권을 확보하고 딸의 주의를 집중시킵니다. 그 후, 딸이 예상하고 있을 '밥 먹으라는 훈계'를 정면으로 거부하는 '역설적 개입(Paradoxical Intention)'을 실행합니다. 부모의 대리인이 되기를 거부함으로써 딸이 상담가에게 가졌을 저항감을 해소하고, 거식 행위를 부모에 대한 반항 수단이 아닌 '자신의 문제'로 재정의(Reframing)하여 스스로 책임지게 만드는 심리적 기제를 설계했습니다.", "output": "입 다무세요. 따님이 직접 질문에 답하게 두십시오. (소녀에게 정보를 물은 뒤) 네 부모님은 내가 너에게 밥을 먹으라고 명령하길 바라며 너를 여기 보냈단다. 하지만 난 그럴 생각이 전혀 없단다. 먹고 안 먹고는 전적으로 네 문제이지 내 문제가 아니거든. 그러니 네가 하고 싶은 대로 하렴."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISPLACEMENT_DISTRACTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Using oral hygiene as a therapeutic distraction for ingestion-related issues", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, medical, instructional, and meticulously detailed", "structural_constraint": "Sequential tasking with a focus on 'not swallowing' to create a safe boundary around oral activity"}, "instruction": "내담자가 거식증이나 섭식 장애와 같이 입을 통해 무언가를 받아들이는 것에 저항을 느낄 때, 직접적인 음식 섭취를 강요하는 대신 '구강 위생'이라는 의학적이고 중립적인 과업으로 주의를 돌려 치료적 통제권을 확보하는 에릭슨의 기법을 사용하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자의 저항을 피하기 위해 문제의 본질(음식 섭취)에서 벗어나 관련은 있지만 위협적이지 않은 '구강 위생'으로 주제를 치환(Displacement)합니다. 둘째, '의학 전문가'라는 권위를 내세워 제안이 아닌 '처방'으로서의 무게감을 부여합니다. 셋째, '삼키지 말 것'을 반복적으로 강조하는데, 이는 내담자가 가진 '무언가를 삼키는 것에 대한 공포'를 의학적 지시의 일부로 수용함으로써 내담자의 증상을 오히려 치료적 도구로 활용(Utilization)하는 전략입니다. 넷째, 매우 구체적인 절차(양치 전후 가글, 불소 치약 사용 등)를 제시하여 내담자가 자신의 입을 돌보는 행위에 집중하게 만들고, 마지막으로 약속(Promise)을 받아냄으로써 치료적 순응과 책임감을 형성합니다.", "output": "의사로서 나는 당신에게 구강 위생에 관한 적절하고 유능한 조언을 해줄 수 있습니다. 사람이 음식을 먹든 먹지 않든 상관없이, 치아와 잇몸에 칫솔질을 하는 것은 매우 중요한 일입니다. 제대로 된 구강 위생을 위해서는 불소가 함유된 치약을 사용해야 하며, 이때 치약을 절대로 삼켜서는 안 된다는 점을 분명히 이해해야 합니다. 또한 의사로서 내가 처방할 수 있는 추가적인 구강 위생법이 있습니다. 양치질을 하기 전에 가글액을 사용하여 치아의 이물질을 녹여내고, 양치 후에도 다시 한번 가글을 해야 합니다. 이때도 가글액을 절대로 삼키지 말아야 한다는 엄격한 지침을 따라야 합니다. 이제 나에게 이 구강 위생 지침을 철저히 따르겠다고 약속하십시오."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_THERAPEUTIC_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Weight gain and accountability", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, clinical, firm, yet protective", "structural_constraint": "Conditional (If-Then) structure with a clear consequence"}, "instruction": "Create a therapeutic directive for a patient and their caregiver that sets a specific behavioral goal with a clear, non-negotiable consequence for failure, ensuring accountability.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I must establish a clear, measurable metric for success—in this case, five pounds in one month—to remove ambiguity and provide a concrete target for the unconscious mind. Second, I need to create a 'therapeutic bind' or a no-lose situation: the patient either succeeds in gaining weight at home (the desired outcome) or returns to my direct supervision (the necessary intervention). Third, by addressing the mother directly with the command 'you will bring her back,' I am mobilizing the family system to act as a co-therapist and enforcer, ensuring the patient cannot manipulate the situation. The tone is intentionally matter-of-fact to present the consequence not as a threat or punishment, but as a logical clinical necessity if the home environment proves insufficient for the patient's recovery.", "output": "If she does not gain five additional pounds in the first month she is home, you will bring her back to me in Phoenix where I will further supervise her."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UNCONSCIOUS_FACILITATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Retrieval of forgotten childhood memories and unconscious reintegration.", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, reassuring, and authoritative yet gentle.", "structural_constraint": "Utilization of truisms, pacing and leading, and incremental suggestion."}, "instruction": "Help the client access forgotten childhood memories by validating the permanence of mental images and suggesting a gradual, pleasurable process of unconscious retrieval.", "reasoning_trace": "I will begin by establishing the permanence of early memories through truisms about the brain's storage. By differentiating between physical cell loss and functional memory retention, I bypass conscious skepticism. I will then frame the recovery process as a source of pleasure rather than a task, using the 'one small step' approach to lower resistance. Finally, I will delegate the pacing to the client's unconscious mind, reinforcing the idea that the unconscious is an autonomous, capable entity that knows the perfect speed for this integration.", "output": "But the mental images that you formed in kindergarten are still within your mind. Things long forgotten still have their mental images in your mind. You can lose learnings by the loss of brain cells. But you haven't lost the brain cells concerned with your delivery. [Pause] And those mental images belong to you, and you can enjoy getting them back. And I think the best way of getting them back is doing so by getting one small one and being completely delighted by it. Not asking for more, but just enjoying the pleasure and delight of that one little memory. And the next thing you know you'll get another little memory that will give you a great deal of pleasure and delight. And doing it this way you will build up your pleasure and comfort and ease very rapidly. Not rapidly in time but rapidly in force, in strength. And then some day you'll realize you really do have all of it. And when one uses the unconscious mind, one does it at the rate of speed that belongs to the unconscious. Your unconscious knows how fast it can work, how fast your conscious mind works. And your unconscious will know how to feed that memory back to you."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_OWNERSHIP_RECLAMATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reclaiming lost mental images and memories", "tone_constraint": "Affirmative, empowering, and emotionally evocative", "structural_constraint": "Linking past loss to present recovery while emphasizing the patient's inherent right and emotional reward"}, "instruction": "내담자가 상실감을 느끼는 내적 자원(기억, 심상)에 대해 소유권을 재확립하고, 이를 되찾는 과정에 긍정적인 정서를 결합하여 변화를 유도하는 에릭슨 스타일의 대화를 구성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 잃어버렸다고 느끼는 심상이 사실은 내담자의 소유임을 명확히 선언(Affirmation)하여 심리적 통제권을 부여한다. 과거에 그것들이 '도망쳤다'는 표현을 활용해 내담자의 잘못이 아님을 암시하고, 이제는 그것을 되찾을 '권리(Deserve)'가 있음을 강조하여 무의식적 허용을 이끌어낸다. 마지막으로 거창한 기억이 아닌 '작은 기억 하나'가 주는 '기쁨(Delight)'에 집중하게 함으로써, 무의식이 저항 없이 자연스럽게 긍정적인 연합을 형성하고 변화를 수용하도록 유도한다.", "output": "그 정신적 이미지들은 원래 당신의 것이며, 당신은 그것들을 다시 되찾아 누릴 충분한 권리가 있습니다. 예전에 그것들이 잠시 당신을 벗어났던 적이 있었지만, 이제 당신에게 속한 것을 다시 돌려받는 그 즐거움을 느껴보십시오. 아주 작은 기억 하나가 당신에게 줄 수 있는 그 소소하고도 깊은 기쁨에 온전히 집중해 보시기 바랍니다."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_FUTURE_PACING_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Noncritical acceptance of memory and self-integration", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, future-oriented, and reassuring", "structural_constraint": "Temporal shift using 'Someday' to bypass immediate ego-resistance"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 기억을 비판 없이 수용하고 내면의 자원을 통합할 수 있도록 돕는 최면적 암시를 구성해 주세요.", "reasoning_trace": "내담자의 현재 자아 비판(Self-criticism)을 우회하기 위해 '미래 페이싱(Future Pacing)'과 '전제(Presupposition)' 기법을 결합합니다. '언젠가(Someday)'라는 단어는 변화의 시점을 미래로 유예함으로써 현재의 저항을 낮추고, '깨닫게 될 것이다(will realize)'라는 표현은 그 변화가 필연적으로 일어날 것임을 무의식에 심어줍니다. '모든 것을 가졌다는 것(have all of it)'은 파편화된 기억이나 경험들이 이미 내면에 존재하며, 단지 그것을 수용하기만 하면 된다는 암시를 줍니다. 이는 작은 기억 조각 하나하나를 비판 없이 받아들이게 하여, 자아 비판의 메커니즘을 무력화하고 통합된 자아로 나아가게 하려는 의도적인 언어 설계입니다.", "output": "언젠가 당신은 당신이 그 모든 것을 이미 가지고 있었다는 사실을 깨닫게 될 것입니다."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISSOCIATION_CONTRAST", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Separation of conscious and unconscious processes", "tone_constraint": "Analytical, instructional, and authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Direct meta-commentary on therapeutic technique"}, "instruction": "Explain your method for separating a patient's conscious and unconscious minds during a session, specifically using the concept of processing speed.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate deep therapeutic change, I must create a functional dissociation between the patient's conscious ego and their unconscious resources. I start by attributing 'knowledge' and 'agency' to the unconscious, suggesting it has an inherent understanding of its own internal tempo. By stating 'it belongs to the unconscious,' I am linguistically reassigning the problem-solving responsibility away from the patient's often-stuck conscious mind. I then introduce a contrast—comparing the rapid, autonomous speed of the unconscious with the slower, more limited speed of conscious thought. This comparison forces the patient's mind to recognize two distinct operating systems within themselves. This structural separation is not just a description; it is an intervention that allows the unconscious to work independently of conscious interference or skepticism.", "output": "Yes, I say it belongs to the unconscious and the unconscious knows how fast it works. The second step is to empower the patient's subjective reality. By saying 'I let her own experience define it,' I am utilizing whatever internal phenomena she is encountering as the valid foundation for therapy. This approach bypasses resistance because there is no external definition to fight against; the patient's own experience becomes the ultimate authority, making the therapeutic process inherently authentic to her unique unconscious mind.", "output": "I didn't define it as trance. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_ANCHORING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Strategic memory recovery through temporal anchoring and ego-strengthening", "tone_constraint": "Analytical, empowering, and clinical yet deeply humanistic", "structural_constraint": "Direct explanation of the psychological mechanism behind the therapeutic intervention"}, "instruction": "Explain the psychological rationale for using a specific, known memory as a 'marker' to facilitate the recovery of lost or repressed memories in a clinical setting.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate memory recovery, I must first identify a 'stable island' within the patient's fragmented consciousness. By utilizing a specific time—6:40—that the patient already recalls clearly, I create a psychological anchor. This anchor serves as a non-threatening starting point for the unconscious mind to begin the process of association. The strategy is to move from the 'known' to the 'unknown' by providing a structural framework (a marker) that the patient previously lacked. Furthermore, I must diminish my own role as the therapist to avoid creating dependency; by framing myself as the 'background' and the patient's experience as the 'foreground,' I return the ownership of the memory to the patient. This empowers the patient to restructure their own recall naturally, following the implied suggestion that their experience is their own property to reclaim.", "output": "I'm giving her a base within her own experience. When she lost her memories, she never really tried to restructure her recall as I'm now suggesting. When she now begins to recount the circumstances of how her water bag broke, she is following my implied suggestion where I've been telling her all along, This is your experience. It belongs to you. I'm only a background. Your own experience is the foreground."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_OF_CHANGE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Recognizing and reinforcing the patient's psychological maturation", "tone_constraint": "Observational, calm, authoritative yet gentle, and subtly validating.", "structural_constraint": "Initial general observation followed by a specific exclusion of physical traits, concluding with a focus on internal and behavioral markers of growth."}, "instruction": "내담자의 내면적 성숙과 변화를 관찰하고 이를 무의식적으로 강화하기 위한 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하세요. 신체적 변화가 아닌 언어적 표현과 사고의 구조적 변화에 초점을 맞춰야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 변화를 인지(Observation): 내담자가 이전보다 성숙해졌음을 감지하고 이를 언어화하여 변화를 고착화시키고자 함. 2. 저항 방지(Reframing/Exclusion): '나이가 들었다'는 표현이 외모의 노화로 오해받아 부정적 저항을 일으키지 않도록 '외모가 아니다(Not in looks)'라고 즉각적으로 선을 그음. 3. 무의식적 지표 활용(Focusing on Unconscious Markers): 내담자가 의식적으로 통제하기 어려운 '목소리의 울림(sound of speech)', '태도(manner)', '사고의 배치(arrangement of ideas)'를 언급함. 이는 내담자의 무의식적 성장을 거울처럼 비춰주는 기법임. 4. 점진적 수용(Subtle Suggestion): 'slightly(약간)'라는 부사를 사용하여 내담자가 거부감 없이 이 변화를 자신의 새로운 정체성으로 받아들이게 유도함. 5. 통합(Integration): 사고의 구조가 변했다는 점을 강조함으로써 치료적 진전이 내면 깊숙이 자리 잡았음을 암시함.", "output": "You appear slightly older now. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONSCIOUS_UNCONSCIOUS_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Explaining the therapeutic focus on the unconscious over conscious resistance", "tone_constraint": "Direct, authoritative, yet dissociative and non-confrontational", "structural_constraint": "Simple declarative sentences that create a clear boundary between two mental states"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 저항이나 망설임에 대해 의문을 제기할 때, 의식적인 논쟁을 피하고 의식과 무의식을 분리하여 무의식의 소통에만 집중하겠다는 에릭슨 특유의 접근 방식을 표현하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자의 '왜(Why)'라는 질문은 의식적인 분석과 저항을 유도하므로, 이에 대해 논리적으로 설명하기보다 의식 자체를 우회(Bypass)해야 한다고 판단함. 둘째, '의식(Conscious mind)'과 '무의식(Unconscious)'을 명확히 대조시키는 이분법적 언어를 사용하여 내담자의 주의를 분산시킴. 셋째, 의식에 자극을 주지 않겠다는 선언을 통해 내담자의 방어 기제를 무력화하고, 무의식의 반응이 더 가치 있다는 암시를 주어 내담자가 스스로의 내면에 집중하게 만듦. 넷째, 'I prefer'라는 주관적 선호의 표현을 사용하여 치료적 권위를 유지하면서도 내담자의 무의식적 자율성을 존중하는 역설적 프레임을 구축함.", "output": "I'm not going to prompt your conscious mind. Crucially, I will link the act of awakening with the internal state of 'comfort and pleasure' through a process of association: as the level of consciousness increases, the level of pleasure must also increase. Finally, I will conclude with a short, direct, and universal command—'Enjoy life'—to plant a positive posthypnotic seed that extends beyond the session.", "output": "Now straighten up still some more. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_VALIDATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The relationship between physical awareness and psychological inquiry", "tone_constraint": "Calm, validating, and subtly indirect", "structural_constraint": "A concise, declarative sentence focusing on the positive state of current knowledge."}, "instruction": "Respond to a client who is questioning the relevance of their physical sensations to your previous therapeutic inquiry. Use a validating truism that shifts the focus from their confusion to their existing capacity for understanding.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Analyze the client's query: The client is seeking a logical or intellectual connection between a specific body part (breasts) and the therapeutic process. 2. Determine the therapeutic objective: Avoid a direct, analytical explanation which might lead to intellectualization or resistance. Instead, reinforce the client's sense of self-efficacy and awareness. 3. Utilize the 'Truism' technique: State a universal truth that is impossible to disagree with, creating a 'yes-set' in the unconscious mind. 4. Focus on 'Utilization': Instead of addressing what she doesn't understand, highlight the value of what she *does* understand. 5. Linguistic phrasing: Use the word 'nice' to provide a positive emotional anchor and 'do understand' to emphasize the present state of competence, thereby bypassing the need for immediate logical justification.", "output": "It's nice to know what you do understand."}

'Apparently'라는 부드러운 부사로 문장을 시작하여, 치료자의 주관적 판단이 아닌 객관적 관찰에 의한 당연한 결론인 것처럼 제시함. 3. 'be-yourself way'라는 표현을 통해 내담자의 독특한 개성을 긍정하고, 그것이 교육을 통해 훼손되지 않았음을 강조함. 4. 'never limited'라는 표현을 사용하여 내담자의 행동적 자유를 무의식에 각인시키며, 현재의 무의식적 반응이 그 자유로움의 연장선상에 있음을 암시함. 5. 이를 통해 내담자가 자신의 무의식적 반응에 대해 가질 수 있는 의구심이나 저항을 제거하고, 그것을 자신의 본질적인 강점으로 수용하게 만듦.", "output": "Apparently you were trained in a be-yourself way. Your education never limited your behavior."}

Identify the core psychological mechanism: The act of 'blocking out' is a common defense mechanism. 2. So often you hear people say, I wouldn't even think about that, and they don't."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TOTAL_COMMITMENT_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Airplane phobia treatment and the establishment of therapeutic compliance.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet permissive, utilizing psychological leverage and gender dynamics.", "structural_constraint": "Sequential escalation from conscious agreement to unconscious commitment via trance."}, "instruction": "Explain the initial therapeutic setup for a client with a severe phobia, emphasizing the necessity of an absolute, unconditional commitment that transcends moral or physical boundaries.", "reasoning_trace": "To bypass the client's resistance, I first established a high-stakes psychological contract by framing the commitment as a choice between an unknown ordeal and her current suffering. I utilized the inherent tension of our gender roles and my physical state to create a unique interpersonal pressure. By forcing her to verbalize this promise in both a conscious and a trance state, I ensured that her unconscious mind was fully aligned with the therapeutic process, effectively making her phobia the lesser of two evils.", "output": "I requested an absolute commitment from Mrs. A that she must agree to do anything I asked. If you only knew how grudgingly she gave that promise; she did not enjoy giving it, but she gave it. She thought about it for seven or eight minutes and finally said, no matter what you do to me, it couldn't be worse than that awful fear. Then I put her in a trance and went through the whole thing again until I got the same promise when she was in a trance."}

In everyday life, you may accept an invitation for dinner, and later your unconscious lets you forget it."}

Of course, you'll have some question about it. When you get back to Phoenix from Dallas, you will have discovered how beautiful it is to ride a plane. You will really enjoy it. When you reach Phoenix airport on your return, call me up and tell me how you enjoyed it."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_SYMBOLIC_ANCHORING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reinforcing therapeutic change through physical symbolic anchors", "tone_constraint": "Narrative, clinical yet imaginative, authoritative, and reassuring", "structural_constraint": "A sequence of actions involving physical objects (photographs) paired with specific hypnotic labels to externalize internal processes."}, "instruction": "내담자가 단 한 번의 최면(single trance)으로 얻은 변화를 의심하지 않고 영구적으로 유지할 수 있도록, 시각적 매개체와 은유적 라벨링을 결합하여 무의식에 강력한 이정표를 심어주는 에릭슨의 전략적 개입 방식을 기술하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 단발성 최면의 효과를 공고히 하기 위해 내담자의 시각적 감각을 활용하기로 결정함. 의자라는 일상적 사물을 '문제가 머무는 장소'로 정의하고, 사진의 노출 정도(과다, 부족, 정상)를 심리적 상태의 변화 과정에 대입함. '부족한 노출'은 문제의 소멸을, '과다 노출'은 문제의 파멸을, '정상 노출'은 문제의 영구적 안착(격리)을 상징하게 하여 각기 다른 봉투에 담아 보냄으로써 내담자가 물리적으로 이 변화를 수용하게 함. 마지막으로 '성 크리스토퍼 메달'이라는 은유를 통해 이 사진들이 단순한 종이가 아닌, 내담자를 보호하는 강력한 심리적 부적(anchor)임을 무의식에 각인시킴.", "output": "I then wondered what I should do to be sure of the effectiveness of that single trance. I had my daughter take three pictures of that chair - one picture overexposed, one that was underexposed, and one that was normally exposed. I labeled the one that was underexposed, Where your phobia and troubles rest and are dissipating into nothingness. The overexposed photo, where only the outline of the chair was darkly visible, I labeled, Where your problems are sinking into the gloom of total doom. The normal exposure was labeled The permanent resting place of your problem. I sent her those photos each in separate envelopes. They are her St. Christopher's medal."}

By labeling this behavior as 'ridiculous,' I am actually highlighting the autonomy of the unconscious mind; it continues to follow the therapeutic 'rules' even when the conscious mind finds them peculiar. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISSOCIATIVE_INTEGRATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Separating emotional and intellectual content for therapeutic integration.", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, clinical, and process-oriented with a focus on unconscious mechanisms.", "structural_constraint": "Sequential procedure utilizing repeated trance inductions (fractionation) to bypass resistance."}, "instruction": "Explain the therapeutic technique of separating and then reintegrating emotional and intellectual components of a memory using trance, emphasizing why this bypasses resistance.", "reasoning_trace": "The core strategy is to bypass the patient's inability to face the 'meaningfulness' of a whole experience by breaking it down into manageable parts. I start with a truism about human behavior—crying or feeling elated without knowing why—to establish the reality of unconscious processes and the natural dissociation already present in human experience. Then, I outline a three-stage trance process: first, isolating the emotion to allow recognition without intellectual clutter; second, isolating the intellect while 'burying' the emotion to prevent the patient from being overwhelmed; and third, a final synthesis. This fractionation allows the unconscious mind to process the experience in bite-sized pieces before achieving a complete, integrated memory upon awakening.", "output": "You separate the emotional and intellectual content because so often people cannot face the meaningfulness of an experience. People cry and do not know why they cry, they feel suddenly elated and know not why. In using regression therapeutically you first recover the emotions in trance to help the patient recognize them. Then put the patient back in a trance; this time leave the emotions buried and let the intellectual content be recognized. Then put them back in a trance a third time and put the cognitive and emotional aspects together and then have them come out of trance with a complete memory."}

Once the patient reaches the threshold of ten, I shift to a slow, deliberate single-digit countdown. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_POST_HYPNOTIC_SUGGESTION_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Preparing for a safe retrieval of a traumatic or scary memory", "tone_constraint": "Calm, authoritative yet permissive, structured", "structural_constraint": "Sequential logic (When X happens, Y will follow), followed by reassurance/agreement checks"}, "instruction": "과거의 두려운 기억을 감정적 고통 없이 떠올릴 수 있도록 유도하는 사후 최면 암시(Post-hypnotic suggestion)와 정서적 해리(Dissociation) 기법을 사용하여 환자에게 지시를 내리세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 사후 최면 암시(Post-hypnotic Suggestion) 설정: '다음에 깨어날 때'라는 특정 시점을 트리거로 설정하여 최면 상태가 끝난 후에도 무의식이 작동하도록 설계함. 2. 행동적 고착(Behavioral Anchoring): '예'라고 대답하게 함으로써 환자의 순응성을 강화하고 긍정적인 심리적 상태를 유도함. 3. 정서적 해리(Emotional Dissociation) 유도: '기억은 떠오르지만 감정은 느끼지 않는다'는 암시를 통해 과거의 공포로부터 현재의 자아를 분리함. 이는 내담자가 트라우마적 사건을 객관적으로 관찰할 수 있게 함. 4. 허용적 종결(Permissive Closing): '괜찮겠습니까?'라는 질문을 반복하여 내담자의 저항을 최소화하고, 무의식적 동의를 얻어 암시의 효과를 확고히 함.", "output": "Now the next time I awaken you, A, I have a different kind of task for you. When next I ask you casually if you are awake, you will say 'yes,' and then there will come to your mind something that could have scared you years ago. But you won't feel any emotions at all, is that all right? It won't scare you, is that all right?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PERMISSION_PROTECTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Therapeutic technique for patient protection and consent during trauma exploration", "tone_constraint": "Analytical, protective, and meta-communicative", "structural_constraint": "Direct explanation of clinical intent behind specific linguistic choices and non-verbal cues"}, "instruction": "Explain the strategic use of permission-seeking and rhythmic pauses in your therapeutic approach to accessing a patient's past.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate a safe exploration of a patient's history, I must first transfer the locus of control to them. By asking 'Is that all right?', I am not merely seeking information but establishing a contract of safety. This minimizes the risk of re-traumatization by ensuring the patient is a willing participant in the process. Furthermore, I recognize that communication occurs in the spaces between words as much as in the words themselves. By intentionally placing pauses, I create rhythmic intervals that act as non-verbal reassurances. Each silence is an independent message of protection, signaling that I am present, attentive, and guarding their well-being. This multi-layered approach—combining verbal agreement with structural reassurance—ensures that the patient feels psychologically held throughout the process of disclosure.", "output": "I ask for her approval to view the past when I ask, Is that all right? I describe what she is to do and get her agreement. Each pause in my final sentence is an independent message saying that I will protect her. Each part is a separate reassurance."}

Second, I embed suggestions of physical well-being, specifically using words like 'rested' and 'comfortable', to ensure the subject associates the therapeutic session with a positive physiological state. Third, I establish a specific behavioral trigger: the verbal response 'yes' to the question of being awake is linked directly to the cognitive event of a 'vivid flash' of memory. This ensures that the recall is not a slow effort but a spontaneous unconscious emergence. Finally, I conclude with a permissive tag question, 'Is that all right?', which bypasses conscious resistance by seeking a simple agreement to the structured process I have just laid out.", "output": "Your first look at the clock. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_INTEGRATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Clarifying the integration of intellectual and emotional recall", "tone_constraint": "Reassuring, authoritative, and integrative", "structural_constraint": "Use of pacing phrases like 'That's right' followed by repetitive reinforcement of 'completeness' to bridge the gap between knowing and feeling."}, "instruction": "Provide a response that helps a client integrate their intellectual understanding with their emotional experience regarding past memories, using Milton Erickson's style of reinforcement and holistic integration.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I will use 'That's right' as a pacing technique to validate the client's internal process and create an immediate 'yes-set'. Second, I will address the client's confusion between 'knowing' and 'feeling' by framing them not as opposites, but as components of a 'complete' experience. I will repeat the word 'complete' to suggest a sense of wholeness. Third, I will use temporal anchoring ('then') to allow the client to observe their past self from a safe distance while maintaining full access to the data of that experience. Second, I will introduce the concept of 'Dissociation' by framing memory not as a single unit, but as a composite of emotional and intellectual layers. Third, I use the linguistic bridge 'Even though' to create a transition from the patient's current comfort to the therapist's technical capability. Fourth, I employ a 'Truism' ('you can always') to imply a universal law of the mind, suggesting that the original emotional data remains accessible if needed for further work. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_RESTRUCTURING_EXPERIENCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Restructuring a life experience through behavioral and emotional shifts", "tone_constraint": "Observational, clinical yet hypnotic, permissive, and focused on internal shifts", "structural_constraint": "Contrast between the 'old' habitual state and the 'new' active state to illustrate psychological displacement"}, "instruction": "Explain the process of how a patient overcomes a fear of swimming by contrasting their old habits with new activities, focusing on how new emotions restructure the previous experience.", "reasoning_trace": "I will start by acknowledging the persistence of the 'old' state to establish rapport with the patient's past reality. By describing the patient wading 'halfway into the water,' I am anchoring the old fear to a specific physical context. Then, I will introduce the 'new position'—the act of swimming—as a pattern interrupt. I must emphasize that the fear doesn't just vanish by willpower, but is displaced by the physiological and emotional engagement of the new activity. I will use words like 'potential,' 'generate,' and 'restructure' to suggest that the unconscious mind is actively reorganizing the experience. The goal is to show that while the past remains a possibility, the present activity creates a new emotional reality that modifies the old situation.", "output": "You see, when that patient wades halfway into the water, just as he always did, he can still feel the echoes of that old fear within. It is a familiar sensation in a familiar place. But the moment he takes his new position and begins to swim, something remarkable happens: the old fear simply disappears. While a potential for that old fear remains as a memory, the new activity of swimming generates its own emotions. These new feelings have a way of replacing or restructuring the old experience, so that the very same situation is modified into something entirely different."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_STRATEGIC_SEQUENCING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The hierarchy of therapeutic experience and the sequence of emotional/intellectual integration.", "tone_constraint": "Clinical, strategic, and authoritative regarding the mechanics of the human psyche.", "structural_constraint": "Dualistic framing (giving/taking) followed by a causal explanation of chronological sequencing (emotion before intellect)."}, "instruction": "Explain the rationale behind prioritizing emotional experience over intellectual understanding in a therapeutic setting, adopting Milton Erickson's perspective on how patients integrate change.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate deep change, Erickson recognizes that the conscious intellect often acts as a barrier or a defense mechanism. By framing therapy as a process of 'giving possibilities' and 'taking away undesirable qualities,' he sets up a balanced exchange that reduces resistance. The core strategy here is 'Emotional Primacy.' Erickson reasons that if a patient understands something intellectually first, they may use that logic to avoid the actual felt experience. However, by inducing the emotional experience first, the intensity of the feeling creates a psychological 'tension' or 'need' for resolution. The intellect then steps in not as a defense, but as a tool for integration and closure. This sequence ensures the change is rooted in the unconscious experience before being labeled by the conscious mind.", "output": "We are giving the patient new possibilities and we are taking away the undesirable qualities. Usually it's best to have patients experience the emotion first and later the intellectual, because after they have experienced the emotions so strongly, they have a need to get the intellectual side of it."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISSOCIATIVE_METAPHOR", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Dissociating and reintegrating complex experiences", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, clinical, yet metaphorical and evocative", "structural_constraint": "Sequential logic combined with a physical metaphor (jigsaw puzzle) to explain a psychological process"}, "instruction": "Explain a therapeutic method for dissociating a patient's experience to facilitate safe processing, using a metaphor that emphasizes gradual integration.", "reasoning_trace": "To explain the dissociation of experience, I must first validate the concept of breaking down a complex whole into manageable parts. I will use the 'jigsaw puzzle' metaphor because it perfectly illustrates how individual pieces (facets) can be viewed without revealing the entire picture (the emotional weight) prematurely. By separating emotional facets from intellectual facets, the patient is protected from being overwhelmed. I will emphasize that the 'meaning' or the 'recovery' of the full experience is strategically delayed until the very last piece is placed, ensuring the patient maintains control and safety throughout the therapeutic process. This approach utilizes the principle of fractionation and strategic ambiguity regarding when the 'whole' will be realized.", "output": "Yes. You can have the patient recall one single facet of the emotional experience - then an unrelated intellectual facet, like a jigsaw puzzle. The entire experience can be recovered, the whole meaning can be put together, only when the last piece is put into place."}

Instead of boredom there is a time when you enjoy being within your body, a feeling of resting, feeling of comfort while your mind's eye is exploring the things that really give you pleasure."}

First, I identify a high-energy resource within the patient: her 'strong desire to do good work.' This is her area of competence and psychological power. Second, I identify the area of symptomatic 'weakness': her airplane phobia. Rather than treating the phobia as an isolated pathology, I bridge the two states. By framing the treatment as an extension of her professional excellence, I redirect the momentum of her strength to overwhelm the resistance of her fear. This creates a psychological leverage where her own internal values become the engine for her recovery, making the change feel like a natural extension of her character rather than an external imposition.", "output": "She has a very strong desire to do good work. She is strong there, so I'm using that motivation to deal with the place where she is weak-her airplane phobia."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_REFRAMING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Open and flexible frames of reference through personal anecdote", "tone_constraint": "Reflective, experiential, and multi-layered", "structural_constraint": "Transition from external physical constraint to internal mental expansion"}, "instruction": "신체적 불편함이나 제한된 상황을 마주했을 때, 이를 오히려 내면의 유연한 사고와 무한한 가능성으로 전환하는 밀턴 에릭슨 식의 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여 이야기해 주세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 비행기 안의 좁은 좌석과 시간의 왜곡(저녁 식사 후 바로 아침 식사)이라는 구체적이고 불편한 현실을 언급하여 청자의 현재 상태를 페이싱(Pacing)합니다. 그 후, 이러한 외부적 제약에서 시선을 돌려 '어린 시절의 바다'라는 무한한 공간에 대한 기억으로 주의를 분산(Distraction)시킵니다. I knew we'd arrive in France at breakfasttime, and we'd barely get our dinner eaten before we were handed our breakfast. But throughout that flight I kept thinking about my boyhood concepts of what the ocean was. Its unlimited span, and how that contrasts with my current understanding. I thought about all of my daydreams as a boy and how they had evolved."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_REINFORCEMENT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Academic accomplishment and the internal validation of progress", "tone_constraint": "Encouraging, rhythmic, and hypnotic with a focus on internal sensory experience", "structural_constraint": "Use of parallel clauses starting with 'that you', progressive verb forms, and circular reinforcement of a central theme"}, "instruction": "Create a hypnotic suggestion that reinforces a sense of academic achievement by focusing on the internal feeling of doing a good job and reaching a joyful conclusion.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the desired hypnotic effect, I first anchor the subject to a previous point of progress ('the first change') to establish a narrative of continuous growth. I then utilize nominalization by transforming the act of succeeding into 'a sense of accomplishing,' which allows the subconscious to define its own parameters of success. By employing a rhythmic repetition of 'that you' phrases, I create a pacing effect that leads the subject from the awareness of a task ('have a good job to do') to the active performance ('are doing a good job') and finally to the internal resource state ('reaching in'). The conclusion is designed to anchor the entire academic process to a positive emotional state—'a joyful sense of accomplishment'—ensuring that the memory of the work is inextricably linked to pleasure and fulfillment.", "output": "In going back to the first change, a sense of accomplishing something, of knowing that you have a good job to do, that you are doing a good job, that you are reaching in, that you have concluded with a joyful sense of accomplishment."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_METAPHOR", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Managing fatigue and productivity through task alternation (shifting gears)", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, anecdotal, rhythmic, and authoritative yet gentle", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a personal academic struggle, transitions to physical farm metaphors, generalizes the principle of 'shifting gears', and applies it to the listener's current reality."}, "instruction": "Explain the concept of 'shifting gears' to manage mental and physical fatigue, using personal anecdotes from farm life and academic study to illustrate how alternating tasks provides rest and maintains high performance.", "reasoning_trace": "To effectively teach the concept of 'shifting gears,' I will first establish rapport by sharing a personal vulnerability—my own struggle with a lack of literary knowledge. This makes the listener more receptive. I will then introduce the 'plan' of alternating between novels and textbooks, which serves as a mental model. This 'truism' of physical rest through alternation bypasses conscious doubt. I will then bridge these physical and academic examples to the listener's specific situation (lectures, work, homework), reframing their fatigue not as a total exhaustion, but as a need to 'untense' specific patterns of functioning. By ending with a direct question, I prompt the unconscious mind to integrate this new strategy of 'resting while working.'", "output": "All right, now I'll explain further. I worked out this plan. I borrowed six novels from the library. Because every time you shift from one pattern of physical activity, you rest from the previous activity. On the farm I learned to pitch hay right-handedly and left-handedly. When my right arm got tired, I rested it by using my left hand. In chopping wood - right- and left-handed. Always resting first one arm and then the other. Alternating in hoeing in the garden, I did the same thing. In studying chemistry, it is so different than reading a novel. Reading a novel is one kind of an exercise, and a chapter from a psychology book is another kind of exercise, so I was always working at top speed at each of the things that I was doing and resting from all the other things. Now working all day tires you. Studying your homework at night is also tiring. But to untense that part of your body fatigued by the day's work and work with the rest of you on homework. Listening to lectures is one thing, doing paid work is another thing, and studying is a third type of exercise. You alternate them and understand that you can rest the lecture-receiving apparatus while you're doing homework, and rest from homework activity when you are doing office work. Because it all requires different sets of patterns of functioning. Do you understand?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_METAPHOR_REFRAMING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reframing task anxiety and confusion through professional analogy (surgeon).", "tone_constraint": "Reassuring, authoritative, instructional, and rhythmic.", "structural_constraint": "Validation -> Metaphorical Analogy -> Skill Transfer -> Future Pacing -> Psychological Contrast."}, "instruction": "내담자가 비행이나 주어진 과업에 대해 혼란과 불안을 느낄 때, 숙련된 외과의사의 맹장 수술 비유를 통해 과업에 대한 존중과 세심한 준비의 중요성을 전달하고, 이를 통해 불안을 긍정적인 기대와 정신적 자유로 전환시키는 에릭슨의 대화형 최면 기법을 구사하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 혼란을 '과업의 중요성을 인식하는 과정'으로 재정의(Reframing)하여 심리적 저항을 완화합니다. 이어서 '단순한 맹장 수술'이라는 등가적 비유(Isomorphic Metaphor)를 도입합니다. 숙련된 의사가 수술의 잠재적 위험을 인지하면서도 철저한 준비를 통해 그것을 의도적으로 '단순한 것'으로 만들어가는 과정을 묘사함으로써, 내담자에게 상황에 대한 통제감과 전문적 태도를 무의식적으로 암시합니다. 특히 '당신이 하기 때문에(because you are doing it)' 성공할 것이라는 직접적인 암시를 삽입하여 자아 효능감을 강화합니다. 마지막으로 비행과 준비 과정을 수술의 즐거움과 병치시켜 미래를 긍정적으로 조망하게(Future Pacing) 하며, 지루함이 시야를 좁힌다는 통찰을 제시함으로써 정신적 자유를 선택하도록 유도합니다.", "output": "It's okay, A. Recognizing that the task ahead of you has sufficient proportions to mean a great deal. You look at your work the way a surgeon looks at an operation. It is a simple appendectomy, but if you are a good surgeon, you know that in the United States, quite unexpectedly, a certain number of simple appendectomies die from surgery. Therefore, you know there isn't such a thing as a simple appendectomy. So you set about making it a simple appendectomy. Taking care to omit nothing that is important. And have the good feeling this is going to be a simple appendectomy because you are doing it. A very good surgeon feels just a simple operation and it is going to turn out right because he is not going to omit anything and he is going to enjoy doing it and the patient is going to enjoy having had it done. You give the proper amount of respect to the task in hand, realizing that there are hazards in any human performance, which have to be met by each functioning human being, and then the enjoyment of looking forward to doing it, a simple act of appendectomy tomorrow, looking forward to enjoying that flight tomorrow, looking forward to the enjoyment of preparing whatever it is. And letting that take over boredom. Boredom narrows your vision and restricts the freedom of your mind to think."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_AND_PERSPECTIVE_SHIFT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Finding comfort in perceived adversity through sensory reframing and altitude shifts.", "tone_constraint": "Calm, evocative, storytelling, and philosophically curious.", "structural_constraint": "Begins with grounded sensory pacing (barn, rain), transitions to comparative relief (not pitching hay), and ends with an abstract perspective shift (30,000 feet altitude)."}, "instruction": "When a client views a situation as 'bad' or 'unpleasant,' use sensory-rich storytelling to reframe that situation as a source of comfort and protection. Then, gradually expand their perspective from a grounded, physical reality to a high-altitude, abstract viewpoint to induce a state of curious detachment.", "reasoning_trace": "I will start by pacing the client's experience of 'bad weather' but immediately reframe it as a pleasant sensory event (raindrops on a roof). By placing the listener in a safe, comfortable environment (lying on hay in a barn), I create a 'safe container.' I then use contrast—comparing the rain to the labor of pitching hay in the hot sun—to make the 'bad weather' a symbol of rest. To further deepen the state, I introduce basic physiological satisfactions (good meals) to anchor the feeling of security. Finally, I will lead the client's mind through a vertical perspective shift, moving from 'zero feet' to '30,000 feet.' This dissociation helps the client view their problems from a distance, replacing anxiety with a sense of wonder about how one 'deals with the air' at high speeds, which is a metaphor for navigating life's pressures.", "output": "There is nothing more pleasant than the sound of raindrops on the roof when you are lying on the hay in the barn, knowing at least you won't be out in the hot sun pitching hay. Well, it certainly isn't a blizzard. If it were a blizzard, a blizzard is terrible in so many different ways. And bad weather, 30,000, 35,000 feet up is a different kind of weather than at zero feet. I often wonder, when I was at 30,000 feet above sea level, what would it be like if I could sense how a plane was dealing with that air at that speed."}

'But'이라는 접속사를 사용하여 내담자가 가졌을 법한 부정적인 자기 대화(Self-talk)를 즉각적으로 중단시키고, 'frame of reference'라는 심리학적 용어를 사용해 상황을 객관화합니다. 이는 내담자로 하여금 '내가 잘못한 것이 아니라 단지 도구가 없었을 뿐이다'라는 무의식적 안도감을 느끼게 하며, 새로운 학습을 위한 공백(tabula rasa)을 마련하는 전략적 발화입니다.", "output": "But you had no frame of reference."}

I use the qualifier 'sometimes' to frame the statement as a universal truism, making it impossible to disagree with. I then introduce 'intellectual knowledge' as one component of their experience. Crucially, I use the conjunction 'and' instead of 'but' to link the emotional state to the intellectual one; this prevents the creation of a psychological barrier or a sense of failure. By describing the emotion as being 'behind it,' I utilize a spatial metaphor that implies a natural sequence. This suggests that the emotion is simply following at its own pace and will eventually catch up, thereby pacing the patient's current experience while leading them toward a future where the two states are synchronized.", "output": "Now sometimes you can have intellectual knowledge of it, and you may be emotionally behind it."}

'지면 위에서(on the ground)'라는 구체적인 물리적 맥락을 제시함으로써 내담자의 의식을 과거의 구체적인 경험으로 유도(Transderivational Search)하며, 질문 형식을 통해 내담자가 스스로 그 연결고리를 무의식적으로 탐색하고 긍정하게 만듭니다.", "output": "The feelings that you learned on the ground?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Fear of air turbulence and the need for a new frame of reference", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, calm, and psychologically insightful", "structural_constraint": "Contrast between ground-based learning and aerial experience with a suggestive command"}, "instruction": "비행 중 난기류에 대한 공포를 느끼는 내담자에게, 그 감정이 지상에서의 학습된 반응임을 인지시키고 공중이라는 새로운 환경에 맞는 올바른 감정 체계를 구축하도록 유도하는 최면적 암시를 제공하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 공포를 '지상에서 학습된 것'으로 규정함으로써 문제의 근원을 현재의 비행 상황이 아닌 과거의 학습으로 분리(Dissociation)시킵니다. '가지고 올라갔다(carried them aloft)'는 표현을 통해 감정이 장소에 부적절하게 이동했음을 암시하여 현재의 공포가 맥락에 맞지 않음을 시사합니다. 마지막으로 '저 위에서 가져야 할 올바른 감정이 무엇인지 알라(Know...)'는 강력한 전제(Presupposition)와 개방형 암시를 사용하여, 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 비행 상황에 적합한 새로운 자원과 평온함을 탐색하고 재구조화(Reframing)하도록 유도하는 전략을 취합니다.", "output": "You learned certain feelings of fear on the ground, and you carried them aloft with you. Know what right feelings you should have up there."}

'Stop to consider'라는 구절은 내담자의 의식적 흐름을 일시 정지시키고 무의식적인 탐색을 유도하는 중단 기법으로 작용합니다.", "output": "Yes. Finally, I add a touch of human vulnerability and humor ('I don't know how they could spit') to dismantle the 'expert' persona, making the profound realization more accessible and less threatening to the ego.", "output": "Total unknowns! Now what I'm telling you is that air turbulence can't be understood in terms of ground experience, just as the astronauts found out they couldn't understand the absence of gravity. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_PARADOX", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Acknowledging the limits of one's own knowledge", "tone_constraint": "Humble, calm, and paradoxical", "structural_constraint": "Short, self-referential statement using meta-cognition"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 관점에서, 상담자가 모든 것을 알지 못한다는 내담자나 관찰자의 지적에 대해 무의식적인 신뢰를 구축할 수 있는 방식으로 대답하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 내담자의 저항이나 비판적 관찰을 직면했을 때 이를 부정하기보다 '활용(Utilization)'하는 전략을 취합니다. 이 문장은 단순한 사실의 나열처럼 보이지만 고도로 계산된 심리적 장치입니다. 첫째, '모른다'는 사실을 인정함으로써 상대방의 비판적 사고(Critical Factor)를 우회하고 라포(Rapport)를 형성합니다. 둘째, '내가 모른다는 사실을 알고 있다'는 메타 인지적 표현을 통해, 무지가 통제되지 않는 결점이 아니라 명확히 인식되고 관리되는 영역임을 암시합니다. 셋째, '안다(Know)'와 '모른다(Don't know)'를 교차 배치하여 논리적 혼란을 야기함으로써 내담자를 가벼운 트랜스 상태로 유도하고, 상담자의 정직함에 대한 무의식적 신뢰를 강화합니다.", "output": "There are a lot of things that I know I don't know."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANALOGY_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The necessity of new measurements for psychological growth", "tone_constraint": "Observational, conversational, and authoritative yet gentle", "structural_constraint": "Begins with a scientific fact to establish credibility, transitions into a relatable developmental metaphor, and concludes with a psychological anchor of success."}, "instruction": "Explain the concept of psychological growth and the need for new ways to measure progress by using a combination of scientific trivia and common developmental experiences, mirroring Milton Erickson's conversational style.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the desired psychological effect, I first establish a 'Yes-Set' by referencing a factual, scientific observation about astronauts. This engages the conscious mind with logical data while subtly introducing the idea that physical measurements are fluid and dependent on context. I then bridge this to a deeply relatable human experience—a child's growth spurt. By using the phrase 'You know what happens,' I employ a truism that invites the listener to subconsciously agree and access their own memories of growth and pride. The comparison of the child to the mother serves as a metaphor for the client's progress relative to their previous limitations. Finally, I anchor the feeling of achievement with the exclamation 'How tall I am!', suggesting that significant internal change eventually becomes an undeniable external reality recognized by everyone, thereby validating the client's potential for transformation.", "output": "You know the measurements show that the astronauts grew one inch in space, and they lost that inch very promptly after reaching the earth. '서투른 단계가 곧 성장하는 단계'라는 명제를 통해 현재의 고통이나 혼란을 성장의 필수 증거로 재프레임(Reframing)합니다. 아이가 자신의 몸을 다시 측정해야 하듯, 내담자 또한 현재의 혼란(난기류) 속에서 새로운 심리적 기준을 세워야 함을 암시합니다. 마지막에 '난기류(turbulence)'라는 단어를 도입하여 은유를 내담자의 실제 문제로 연결하고, 개방형 질문을 통해 무의식이 스스로 새로운 대처 기제(measurements)를 탐색하도록 유도합니다.", "output": "He was bumping into things! Now what set of measurements will you form for turbulence?"}

'성장하는 시기(growing age)'와 '어색한 시기(awkward age)'를 등치시킴으로써 현재의 부적응 상태가 사실은 발달의 증거임을 암시함. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_FEEDBACK", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The strategic use of multiple examples and observation in therapy", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, authoritative, and focused on subconscious resonance", "structural_constraint": "Direct explanation of meta-therapeutic techniques involving patient experience"}, "instruction": "Explain the rationale behind providing multiple examples to a patient and the importance of observing their response from the perspective of Milton Erickson.", "reasoning_trace": "To explain this therapeutic strategy, I must first acknowledge the uniqueness of each patient's internal world. My reasoning follows these steps: 1. Recognize that a single example may fail if it doesn't align with the patient's specific life history. 2. Therefore, I provide a 'scatter-gun' approach of multiple examples to increase the statistical probability that one will resonate with their subjective experience. 3. I understand that the unconscious mind only 'grabs' or 'clings' to information that it can map onto existing memories or patterns. 4. Finally, I emphasize the necessity of 'calibration'—the therapist must constantly monitor the patient's non-verbal feedback to see which example 'landed,' as this evidence of acceptance is the only way to ensure the therapy is progressing effectively.", "output": "You give many examples so that patients are more likely to find one that's personally convincing and actually helps alter their behavior. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_RESPECT_RESISTANCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Respecting psychological defenses and the ethics of uncovering techniques", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, clinical, yet deeply empathetic and strategically nuanced", "structural_constraint": "Direct pedagogical advice to practitioners involving a subtle linguistic distinction"}, "instruction": "Explain the importance of respecting a patient's psychological defenses while maintaining clinical control, specifically focusing on the distinction between perceived needs and actual needs.", "reasoning_trace": "To address the delicate balance between uncovering trauma and respecting defenses, I must first establish the patient's autonomy as a functional necessity. I will start by validating the 'covered up' material as having a 'very good reason,' which builds immediate rapport and safety. Then, I will introduce a strategic paradox: the therapist openly disagrees with the need for secrecy but promises to 'abide by their needs.' The core of this maneuver lies in the linguistic qualification of 'actual needs.' By emphasizing 'actual needs' versus the patient's perceived need for concealment, I create a space where the patient feels respected and safe, yet the therapist retains the latitude to address the underlying psychological reality that the patient may not yet consciously recognize. This allows the therapist to lead the patient toward health while the patient feels their boundaries are being fully honored.", "output": "In this matter of uncovering techniques I think one of the most important things is to recognize that if your patient has something covered up, she's got it covered up for a very good reason, and you'd better respect that fact. You ask the patients to respect the fact that you personally do not think it needs to be covered up but that you are going to abide by their needs, their actual needs. Now you've told them you will abide by their needs, but they don't hear you qualify it to their actual needs."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_STRATEGIC_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Memory recovery and the separation of intellectual and emotional content", "tone_constraint": "Reassuring, permissive, clinical yet deeply psychological, and authoritative in its logic.", "structural_constraint": "Logical progression from general memory mechanics to specific safety assurances, concluding with a dissociative technique."}, "instruction": "Explain to a patient how they can safely approach traumatic memories by distinguishing between intellectual facts and emotional experiences, while emphasizing their control over the process.", "reasoning_trace": "To help a patient navigate trauma, I first frame the issue as a manageable choice between 'covering' and 'uncovering.' I use the logic of 'collateral covering'—explaining that when we hide a trauma, we accidentally hide many safe, mundane details like the room or the year. This makes the prospect of uncovering less threatening, as most of what is hidden is actually harmless. I then provide a psychological safety net by asking the patient how quickly they could 're-cover' something if they felt unsafe, which reinforces their sense of control. Finally, I introduce the concept of dissociation: the ability to separate the intellectual facts from the emotional weight. By suggesting they can view a memory as a mere fact, 'as if it happened to somebody else,' I allow them to process the information without being overwhelmed by the original pain.", "output": "Yes. You actually have two issues here: Does it need to be covered up? Can it be uncovered? You then point out to a patient that there are various ways of remembering things. Undoubtedly, when we cover up a memory, we usually cover up a lot more than the memory itself. That is, trauma of a shaved head might be covered up as an uncomfortable memory, but along with that would be covered up the room in which it was done, perhaps the address of that particular place, and other things that happened that year. Does the year need to be covered up? All the other things that happened that year? You thus emphasize that the patient undoubtedly covered up many things that didn't need to be covered up. So why not uncover every one of those things that are not safe to uncover and be sure to keep covered up the things that are not safe to uncover? You then define the situation as one from which the patient can withdraw at any time. You point out, Suppose you did accidentally uncover something you didn't want uncovered. How long do you think it would take you to cover it up again? That is the little bit of assurance that you always give your patient. You then point out to a patient that it is perfectly possible to remember the intellectual facts of something but not the emotional content, and vice versa. You point out that once, when you felt downhearted and blue, you couldn't for the life of you figure out why, but there must have been a reason in the back of your mind. You experienced the emotions but you didn't have intellectual content. In recovering a traumatic memory you can uncover deep emotions and not intellectual content. If you want to, you can remember the actual intellectual content; you need not remember whether you felt sad, mad, or glad. It will be just a memory, as if it happened to somebody else."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_METAPHOR_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Recovering repressed or forgotten memories through metaphorical dissociation", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, calm, and permissive, utilizing a deep trance state to bypass conscious resistance.", "structural_constraint": "Uses a complex metaphor (the jigsaw puzzle) to separate the 'meaning' of a memory from its 'structure' or 'foundation'."}, "instruction": "Explain to a subject in a deep trance how they can begin to reconstruct a forgotten memory without feeling overwhelmed by its meaning, using a metaphor that separates emotion from intellect and emphasizes incremental progress.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I must validate the subject's conscious frustration that the memory feels 'unreachable' to lower their defenses. Then, I introduce the jigsaw puzzle metaphor because it represents a complex whole made of manageable parts. I deliberately create a dissociation between the 'picture' (intellectual/repressed content) and the 'back' (emotional foundation/blankness). This allows the unconscious to work on the 'foundation' without the conscious mind being startled by the 'picture'. I suggest assembling it non-linearly—two pieces in one corner, two in another—to mirror how the unconscious mind retrieves information in fragments rather than chronological order. By suggesting some pieces be 'face up' and others 'face down', I am giving the unconscious permission to reveal only what the subject is ready to see, while still completing the structural 'puzzle' of the memory.", "output": "All right, you are in a deep trance. I would like to explain a few things to you. You know what a jigsaw puzzle is? You can put a jigsaw puzzle together in two ways: You put it together right side up, and then you will know what the picture is; you can put it together reverse side up, and there you have just the back of the jigsaw puzzle. No picture on it - just blank-ness and no meaning, but the puzzle would be together. The picture of the jigsaw puzzle is the intellectual content - the meaningful content of the repressed memory. The back of it is the emotional foundation, and that will be without any picture. It is going to be just the foundation. Now you can put that jigsaw puzzle together by putting two pieces on one corner together, two pieces in the middle together, two pieces in another corner together, two pieces in a third corner, two pieces in a fourth corner, and then, here and there, you can put two or three pieces together. You can put some of the pieces together face up, some pieces together face down."}

'feeling better'는 구체적으로 어떻게 나아지는지 명시하지 않음으로써, 내담자의 무의식이 스스로에게 가장 적합한 방식(근육의 이완, 호흡의 안정 등)으로 '나아짐'을 정의하고 실행하도록 허용합니다. 이러한 단순한 문장은 의식의 저항을 최소화하고 무의식에 직접적인 변화의 명령을 전달합니다.", "output": "You are frightened, but feeling better."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PROGRESSIVE_TRANSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reducing fear and inducing deep hypnotic sleep through progressive desensitization", "tone_constraint": "Calm, rhythmic, repetitive, and authoritative yet gentle", "structural_constraint": "Gradual reduction of negative states paired with the incremental amplification of relaxation and trance depth"}, "instruction": "내담자의 공포심을 점진적으로 줄이고 깊은 최면 상태로 유도하기 위해, 부정적인 상태의 소멸과 긍정적인 이완 상태의 확장을 리드미컬하게 반복하는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 생성하라.", "reasoning_trace": "1. **Pacing the Current State**: Start by acknowledging the patient's fear but immediately frame it as diminishing ('less frightened'). This validates their experience while directing it toward change.\n2. **Incremental Shift (The 'Salami' Technique)**: Instead of demanding immediate calm, use a series of small, believable steps. Move from 'less' to 'still less' to 'light' to 'gone'.\n3. **Positive Substitution**: As the negative word ('fright') is repeated with decreasing intensity, introduce and increase the frequency of positive anchors ('better', 'relaxed', 'comfortable').\n4. **Rhythmic Entrainment**: Use repetitive phrasing to create a hypnotic cadence, which bypasses the conscious mind's critical factor and induces a natural trance state.\n5. **Transition to Deepening**: Once the negative emotion is 'gone', pivot the focus entirely to physiological suggestions ('to sleep', 'deeper') to solidify the transition from emotional relief to deep hypnotic trance.", "output": "You are less frightened, you are feeling better; you are less frightened, you are feeling better and relaxed; you are feeling still less frightened and more relaxed and better; less and less fright, more and more relaxed, better; just a light fright, so much better; fright going, going, gone, relaxed, comfortable; all better, ready to relax; to sleep, to relax, to sleep; and deeper, deeper and deeper and deeper asleep."}

'지난주' 혹은 '지난달'로 시간을 왜곡(Temporal Distortion)하여 사건의 시급성과 강도를 낮춥니다. 'Who really cares now?'라는 수사적 질문을 던져 과거 사건의 정서적 영향력을 무력화합니다. 그 다음, 내담자가 자기 자신을 타인처럼 느끼게 하는 해리(Dissociation) 기법을 적용합니다. That young woman was you, and you were scared, but that's all over now. You are here, talking to me about it. Just tell me everything. Just remember I don't know a single little thing about it, so be sure to tell me all even if you think parts are not important"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PARADOXICAL_INTERVENTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Disrupting obsessive demands through paradoxical pacing and the introduction of a mysterious obstacle.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, urgent, and seemingly aligned with the clients' goals to bypass resistance.", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive validation of the clients' stance followed by a dramatic shift to a 'warning' that commands total focus."}, "instruction": "Act as Milton Erickson addressing a couple who are obsessively demanding a specific outcome (like an abortion). Use a paradoxical technique to command their absolute attention by framing a mysterious warning as the only way to ensure they achieve their stated goal.", "reasoning_trace": "To break the couple's obsessive loop, I first use 'pacing' by repeating their own arguments back to them with high intensity. This signals that I have heard them perfectly, which lowers their defensive barriers. Then, I employ a 'pattern interrupt' by demanding silence and introducing a 'threat' to their goal. By framing this threat as something they are 'helpless' against without my guidance, I create a psychological vacuum that they must fill with intense listening. I am not arguing against their choice; instead, I am positioning myself as the protector of their choice, which forces them into a state of focused, suggestible attention (a light trance) to hear the 'secret' I am about to reveal.", "output": "All right, all right, quiet now, quiet - if you want the help you ask.
